## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of time and velocity. In nonlinear oscillator systems, the acceleration depends on restoring forces (often functions of displacement, which relates to integrated velocity) and damping forces (functions of velocity), leading to terms involving powers of v, nonlinear damping, and possibly trigonometric functions of time if driven.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear damping: dv_dt = c0 * v (linear velocity-dependent damping/driving)
- Cubic nonlinearity (Duffing-type): dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (nonlinear restoring force in velocity space)
- Van der Pol damping: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * v**2) * v (nonlinear damping with amplitude-dependent sign change)
- Polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**2 + c2 * v**3 (general polynomial nonlinearity in velocity)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (nonlinear damping with periodic driving)
- Sinusoidal driving: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * v (harmonic forcing with linear damping)
- Harmonic restoring via time: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) (acceleration as sinusoidal function of time for simple harmonic motion)
- Cosine restoring via time: dv_dt = c0 * cos(c1 * t + c2) (phase-shifted harmonic acceleration)
- Damped driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * sin(c2 * t) + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (linear damping with general periodic drive)
- Nonlinear damping with drive: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (Duffing-type with harmonic forcing)
- Quadratic damping: dv_dt = c0 * v * abs(v) (velocity-squared damping preserving sign, approximated as c0 * v**2 for positive v)
- Mixed time-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * v * sin(c1 * t) (parametric excitation term)
- Fifth-order nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * v**5 (higher-order nonlinear oscillator)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power velocity terms (v, v**3, v**5) → conservative or symmetric nonlinear restoring/damping forces
- Terms like (1 - c*v**2)*v → self-sustained oscillation with amplitude limiting (limit cycle behavior)
- Sinusoidal functions of time → periodic driving forces or harmonic restoring forces expressed in time domain
- Products of v with functions of t → parametric excitation or modulated damping
- Even-power velocity terms (v**2, v**4) → asymmetric or rectifying nonlinear forces
- Linear v term with negative coefficient → energy dissipation (damping); positive coefficient → energy injection
- Combination of sin and cos of same frequency in t → general phase-shifted harmonic, reducible to single sinusoid
- Absence of explicit t dependence → autonomous system where acceleration depends only on state variables
